<Text>Just tried this place while waiting for my son. It's a nice change for a quick bite that you can customize. Traditional Vietnamese fare with a modern twist. They even have an option for "Impossible meat" that should appeal to those trying to cut out animal protein or want to try something different.

I had a yummy chicken bowl which was pretty good but the star for me was the spring rolls. A large helping of protein (beef,chicken,pork or Impossible meat) with lettuce and pickled vegetables. The sauce for the roll was not as strong as I'm used too but the relatively light flavor complemented the spring roll without overpowering the delightful mix of textures and flavors contained within.

<user>109971812048679087408</user><user_name>Evan C.</user_name><Date>1569191104969< /Date><Rate>1< /Rate>< text>
There was some internal issue happening when the tech came to install my brand new out of the box RG. He finally got it working but there was some issue he had hooking it up initially.

Then during the first month having it there have been several service interruptions. After calling I was told I could get a credit for 4 days that they could verify interruption of service.

We've constantly had issues with the quality of connection my router is able to maintain to the DNS, Mediacom. This is a Mediacom issue, nothing on our network could cause the DNS to drop suddenly. Apparently Mediacom has some known issue affecting California and Arizona, so my issues are common.

During viewing Netflix or playing an online game the connection will be completely lost. The DNS disappears which forces me to call Mediacom technical support to which we don't really get a good answer as to what is causing this problem.

However, being an IT guy and having encountered similiar issues with Comcast, I can tell you exactly what the problem is: Their fiber router or bridge, depending upon which they use, is malfunctioning. The signal being routed to our neighborhood is getting interrupted by this malfunctioning hardware.

Meanwhile I still have to pay, which to me seems excessive for dealing with these issues, over $60 a month for internet service.< /text>

< Rate>
4< /Rate>
< Text>
Initially, I had a very bad experience with Mediacom the "Service". Their support was typically onpar with other service providers however (in my opinion all cable service providers have pretty bad customer service, but that's not what this is about), the service seemed to be terrible. The HDTV was pixelated and broken, and the internet connection was constantly going down.
You'll notice I've given 4 stars though and the reason is that the problem WASN'T Mediacom. The problem was the wiring in my home. To make a long story short, I found several problems with the wiring. First was the system was being back-fed into itself creating a loop in the system and introducing a large amount of signal "Noise". Additionally, the unused connections were not properly terminated causing reflection can causing even more noise on the line.
I did the legwork of climbing into the attic and ensured that the drops into each room were properly split (in other words, I have the 1 connection coming from the street and 7 drops throughout the house and a cable modem. I purchased a high quality splitter providing enough ports for all 7 drops and cable modem (8 total out ports, 1 in) I ran an independent cable run to each room where I wanted a cable television drop and one run for the cable modem and I installed terminators on all unused drops (they just screw on and are super cheap for a bag of 10. At the end of the day I was reaching internet speeds at just over the advertised 100Mbps my package included and all HDTV channels were now crystal clear making Mediacom a pretty good service in my opinion. Moral at the end of the story is, before tossing stones at Mediacom, check your own wiring to ensure compatibility.< /Text>

< review>
Mediacom is an absolutely terrible internet service provider. My internet is constantly dropping connectivity. I have contacted them numerous times about getting it fixed and they give you the feeling they care and the "warm fuzzy" that they will fix it but they don't. When I call the "number" (1-800 number is all they have) it sends me to India where I argue with a phone tech telling me "your internet seems to working sir" when it clearly isn't! I've actually had them blame my equipment which is top of the line and brand new.

The only other option for internet here in town is Verizon and they only offer dial-up. Mediacom is owned by someone who branched off from a larger service provider (Times-Warner or something) from another big city (LA or something), then began systematically buying all the internet and cable rights in southern California small towns. They have used this "power" to keep bigger and better companies with broadband out, yet they refuse to upgrade their antiquated system and have even denied some small towns internet service at all!

The cut-rate internet and cable provided by this company is absolutely despicable and the poor service provided puts the cherry on top. I've heard other areas of town have more reliable service but there is seemingly no rhyme or reason to this, it's not like I live in the ghetto!

Mediacom needs to have a lawsuit filed against them for generally being a crappy business. If you're moving here chances are you'll get their service but I guarantee you will hate it. Most people go with Mediacom because they have "faster" speeds than Verizon offers.

If you don't need the "speed" for anything but just normal browsing, go with Verizon. Our neighbors have Verizon and they can even stream and play games on it. You've been warned!</review>

The worst ISP and cable service I have ever used, and that includes the old HBO microwave broadcasts. I dropped into Maru as I was walking up Powell St and thought it looked like a nice place. The decor is clean and there's a nice atmosphere.

I was greeted warmly by the staff and seated at the sushi bar where I made conversation with one of the chefs.

Once my sushi was prepared the chef handed it to me over the counter. I have to say I was blown away by the quality. The sushi was beautifully made, and the fish tasted very fresh, unlike some other places I've been.

Fantastic experience with the food, I just wish the service had been more attentive, but it was quite busy and there were some large tables so I'll forgive them.< /text>

Tourists who brave the hillsides of the Union Square vicinity will be rewarded by this Japanese eatery. The interior is reminiscent of a traditional sushi restaurant in Japan, and there's plenty to choose from the offerings of sushi, bento and dinner items. < Name>
Tessa Owens< /Name>
< date>
1512199001634</date>
<rate>1</rate>< Text>
TL;DR - Ripped off, poor service, lied to, awful food :(

My boyfriend and I visited the restaurant after looking up the menus online, and we checked the menus outside the restaurant on Thanksgiving Day (it was closed for the holiday). The menus posted outside and online were the same. When we visited the restaurant the next day the menus seemed to be different, so I asked the waitress if they had changed their menus. She told us that nothing had changed, but asked me to show the menu I had seen online. When I showed it to her, she immediately broke into a loud outburst (which every nearby table could overhear) telling me that there was no way the restaurant could continue serving fish at such a price. That doesn't bother me - we're happy to order off the updated menus, but she didn't need to make such a scene.

We ordered 1 order (2 pieces each) of toro, maguro, halibut, and uni. The halibut and uni were listed as market price, while the toro and maguro were around $6.50 - $7.00 each. Then, we ordered 6 pcs. of oysters (around $14.00) and one order of ebi tempura ($8.50).
- Ebi tempura: only 3 pieces for $8.50? Nothing was of epic high quality, so we didn't appreciate the portion size. This seemed too high for some simple tempura.
- 6 pc. oysters: they served it to us at the end of the meal when the ice bed under the oysters had already melted. This means that they had waited for quite a while before serving us the oysters. The (tiny) oysters were drowning in an overpowering, acidic sauce. I didn't even want to finish the order.
- The sushi was bad, too. The quality of the fish did NOT seem exceptional or even average. It was under-average. The uni was especially bad. We felt sick all day after eating it. The waitress had advertised the uni and halibut as being especially fresh and highly recommended we order it.

Aside from the sub-par food, the worst part of our experience was what happened when we got our bill. It was around $85 (up to $90+ with tip) for 8 pieces of sushi, 3 pieces of shrimp tempura, and 6 tiny oysters. This is ridiculous. When we asked for our itemized receipt, we noticed that the halibut and uni had been listed as $20 EACH. This is $20 for 2 PIECES of sushi while the other sushi prices were nowhere close. We have previously dined at highly rated sushi restaurants in other parts of Canada and the US, and this price (for sushi) was even beyond what we paid at luxurious, high-end sushi restaurants. We don't mind spending the money for quality, we love sushi! We asked our waitress what happened with the bill, and she went on another rampage, talking about the shortage of fish in the USA and the high price of toro and how hard it was to catch fish. Umm.... if that's really the case, then why haven't the prices at the other restaurants risen so high? She kept arguing without listening to what we had to say - we never raised our voices or said anything rude, and politely tried to explain our confusion. She wouldn't listen and didn't budge.

I didn't really want to write such a negative review - I know that restaurants struggle, and that business is hard - but we would have appreciated more courtesy and transparency, as well as more honesty from the waitress.

Specific requests for the restaurant:
- Update your online menus.
- Be transparent about how much "market price" means. If a guest orders something that is listed as "market price", it is common courtesy to inform them of the price.
- Don't complain about how hard it is to catch fish when someone is confused about their bill.< /Text>
